## Session: T-24 Russia accessibility (Feature #382) — PASSING

### Goal
Research-first decision document on how to make pr-top.com reachable from
Russia, where Cloudflare (the production CDN/edge) is RKN-blocked.
Deliverable per the ticket: research spike across three variants
(a) RU mirror, (b) origin-direct subdomain bypassing CF, (c) per-user
SSH/SOCKS5 workaround; legal risk assessment; performance assessment;
decision doc; phase-2 implementation plan; user-facing instructions for
the (c) fallback.

Source customer signal: Misha Drozd interview, 2026-04-19, lines 638-700
of docs/new_fichas/customer-development-meetings/misha_drozd_2026-04-19.md.

### Research summary

(a) RU mirror — REJECTED. Triggers 152-FZ data localisation, FZ-374
    (Yarovaya / SORM / FSB decryption keys), and GDPR Chapter V cross-
    border transfer obligations to a non-adequate third country. Trades
    "some RU users cannot reach us" for "we have an FSB key-escrow
    obligation". Not defensible for a privacy-positioned therapy SaaS.

(b) Origin-direct subdomain (e.g. ru.pr-top.com, grey-cloud A-record at
    Hetzner origin, Traefik router, Let's Encrypt cert) — CHOSEN. ~1
    engineering hour, zero application code change, zero new legal
    exposure, fully reversible behind a single DNS record. Hetzner IPs
    are reachable from RU as of 2026-04 to 2026-05. Performance loss
    from removing CF caching is negligible (PR-TOP is dynamic, static
    bundle under 250 kB). Fallback (b-tier): if a Hetzner /24 is later
    TSPU-blocked, stand up a small VPS in a non-blocked European DC
    (Hostkey FI / AEZA NL / FirstVDS) to terminate TLS and reverse-proxy
    to EU origin.

(c) Per-user SSH SOCKS5 (Misha's recipe: Termux + ssh -D 1080 + SOCKS5
    in Telegram/browser) — DOCUMENTED AS FALLBACK. Doesn't scale (most
    therapists won't run Termux), and a hosted Shadowsocks/Outline
    endpoint would put us under FZ-276 anti-circumvention amendments
    (March 2024). Documentation only, no hosted service.

### Deliverables

1. docs/decisions/0001-russia-accessibility.md (new file, 192 lines):
   ADR with section 1 Context, section 2 Three-options analysis with
   pros/cons/legal notes, section 3 Performance table (Moscow/SPb RTT,
   TLS, bundle, TTI, API roundtrip), section 4 Compliance matrix
   (152-FZ, GDPR Art.9, FZ-374, FZ-276, EU sanctions across all three
   options), section 5 Decision (option b primary, option c fallback),
   section 6 Phase-2 implementation plan with 12 acceptance criteria
   (DNS, Traefik, TLS, CORS/cookies, CSP, RU ASN reachability check
   across Rostelecom/MTS/Beeline/MegaFon/ER-Telecom/Yota, in-app CF
   detection probe + banner, therapist-facing client-onboarding URL
   toggle, bot deep links unchanged, one-line rollback, Umami
   monitoring, b-fallback escalation), section 7 phase-2-fallback
   already delivered, section 8 Risks and review triggers.

2. docs/troubleshooting/russia-access.md (new file, 136 lines):
   user-facing guide in English + Russian. Covers (1) try
   https://ru.pr-top.com first, (2) browser proxy / WARP / Opera
   built-in VPN, (3) use the bot for bot-capable workflows,
   (4) full SSH SOCKS5 recipe (Termux on Android with F-Droid,
   ssh -D 1080 on Windows/macOS/Linux, Telegram SOCKS5 settings,
   Kiwi/Bromite for Android browser), (5) network switch.
   Includes client-flow guidance and an escalation path
   (support@pr-top.com with city/ISP/error) feeding the ADR section 8
   review trigger.

### Mapping to original feature acceptance steps

  Step 1 (variants a/b/c spike)        section 2 of ADR
  Step 2 (legal risk RU hosting)       section 4 + section 2(a) detail
  Step 3 (performance without CF)      section 3 of ADR
  Step 4 (decision + plan)             section 5 + section 6 of ADR
  Step 5 (if a/b: phase-2 ticket)      section 6 of ADR (12-point AC
                                        for the orchestrator to file
                                        as a new infra ticket)
  Step 6 (if c: user instructions)     docs/troubleshooting/
                                        russia-access.md (EN + RU)

### Verification

This is a research-first feature; deliverable is documentation. No code
changes, so lint / type-check / server-restart / mock-data-grep are not
applicable. Both files are valid Markdown, render correctly, and
cross-reference each other (ADR section 7 points to troubleshooting doc;
troubleshooting doc points to ADR section 8 review trigger).

### Files added
  docs/decisions/0001-russia-accessibility.md     (new file, 192 lines)
  docs/troubleshooting/russia-access.md           (new file, 136 lines)

### Phase-2 follow-up

A separate Infrastructure ticket should be filed by the orchestrator
covering the 12-point Phase-2 acceptance criteria from ADR section 6.
Out of scope for #382, which is research-only.

### Current status
- Feature #382: PASSING (T-24 Russia accessibility — decision doc adopts
  option (b) origin-direct subdomain ru.pr-top.com bypassing Cloudflare,

## Session: T-23 Zoom / Google Meet SDK integration (Feature #381) — PASSING

### Goal
Research-first XL ticket. Customer signal: Алексей Фомкин interview
(docs/new_fichas/customer-development-meetings/fomkin 2026-04-20.md,
lines 181-213) — "from the dashboard window, click and Google Meet or
Zoom opens, you run the session and everything is recorded." Per the
ticket, Phase 1 deliverable is a research spike + decision doc covering
(a) Zoom Meeting SDK vs (b) Zoom Video SDK vs (c) Google Meet vs
(d) RecallAI 3rd-party, with cost / hosting / legal / decision sections.
Code is explicitly out of scope until the ADR clears go.

### Decision summary (full reasoning in ADR)

**No-go for current cycle. Adopt option (e) — status quo on the existing
T-07 / T-19 / T-20 chain plus a one-page user guide on how to record
inside Zoom/Meet/Teams and drag the file into the Bulk Upload page.**

The same interview turn (lines 193-213) explicitly accepts the
post-hoc upload-and-auto-link path as the acceptable fallback ("даже если
вот такой интеграции невозможно ... файлы есть метаданные ... этот файл
присоединится к той сессии"). T-07 (admin upload), T-19 (single-track
diarisation), T-20 (auto-link by date/metadata) — all already merged on
dev — collectively ship that workflow, so the dependency chain the
ticket calls out is satisfied.

**Why each SDK option was rejected:**

(a) Zoom Meeting SDK — embed Zoom UI in dashboard via
    `@zoom/meetingsdk`. Free SDK but requires therapist Zoom Pro
    ($14.99/mo, theirs); 50-80 eng-hours; needs Zoom Marketplace
    approval; Zoom Cloud recording lag is 30-60 min vs. our existing
    drop-and-go; Zoom is RU-blocked which would re-introduce the
    accessibility problem ADR-0001 just solved.

(b) Zoom Video SDK — white-label PaaS video. ~150-250 eng-hours; we
    become a video conferencing company; loses the familiar Zoom UX
    therapists already have.

(c) Google Meet — no JavaScript SDK exists for embedding Meet in a
    third-party origin. Workspace Add-ons SDK runs *inside* Meet
    (wrong direction). Meet REST API can post-fetch artefacts but
    requires Workspace Business Standard ($12/user/mo, theirs) and
    delivers the same tab-switch UX as today.

(d) Recall.ai — third-party meeting bot. Single integration covers
    Zoom/Meet/Teams/Webex; ~3-5 days eng. BUT (i) ~$9.20/therapist/
    month at 16 sessions × 50 min × $0.69/hr — kills Basic-tier
    margin; (ii) bot is visible to client as a participant — privacy
    regression for the paranoid-client / psychoanalyst segment that
    drove T-06 Solo mode; (iii) adds first ever 3rd-party processor
    of Class A audio, full GDPR Art.28(2) sub-processor notice
    machinery.

**Phase-3 deferred trigger conditions (file new ticket only when ALL
fire):**
1. ≥3 paying therapists explicitly request the integration (currently 1:
   Алексей, who explicitly said "если возможно" + accepted fallback).
2. Subscription product has a Premium tier whose unit economics absorb
   ~$10-15/therapist/month of bot-recording cost.
3. Compliance budget for Art.28(2) sub-processor onboarding (DPA, 30-day
   notice, processor list update, T-18 consent text update).

**If/when triggered: Recall.ai is the recommended path** — single
integration, multi-platform, no per-therapist license dependency.
Detailed 8-point Phase-3 implementation outline is in ADR § 6.

### Mapping to original feature acceptance steps

  Step 1 (Zoom Meeting SDK vs Video SDK vs RecallAI)
        -> ADR § 2 (a) (b) (d), full pros/cons each
  Step 2 (license cost comparison)
        -> ADR § 3 cost table (5 rows, build-h + runtime + license dep)
  Step 3 (hosting requirements: server-side bot vs client-side embed)
        -> ADR § 2 implementation outlines for (a) and (d)
  Step 4 (legal: consent in different jurisdictions)
        -> ADR § 4 compliance matrix (GDPR Art.9/28, US two-party
           consent CA/FL/IL/MD/MA/NV/PA/WA, HIPAA BAA availability,
           RU 152-FZ accessibility, FZ-374)
  Step 5 (decision doc go/no-go + scope)
        -> ADR § 5 (no-go for current cycle, defer to Phase-3)
  Step 6 (if go: phase 2 ticket)
        -> ADR § 6 8-point Recall.ai implementation outline (parked
           for orchestrator to file as new Integration ticket once
           triggers fire)
  Step 7 (if no-go: document reason and close)
        -> ADR § 5 rationale + § 7 risks-of-doing-nothing + § 8
           review trigger

### Deliverables

1. docs/decisions/0002-zoom-meet-integration.md (new file, 274 lines):
   ADR with sections 1 Context (with verbatim Russian customer quotes
   + status of T-07/T-19/T-20 dependency chain), 2 Five-options

## Session: T-09 Personal knowledge base / RAG (Feature #367) — PASSING

### Goal
Pro/Premium therapists upload professional reference material (textbooks,
articles, school-specific literature). The AI uses semantically relevant
top-k chunks as additional context during session summarization and NL
queries. Reuses existing vector_embeddings store with source_type='kb'.
AutoForge model: Opus 4.7 (new AI-pipeline w/ RAG + vector embeddings +
async ingest).

### What was built (verification + tying off)

Implementation was complete from prior sub-session work. This session
verified the full end-to-end stack and marked the feature passing.

### Backend pieces verified

1. Migration: src/backend/src/db/connection.js lines 1508-1551
   - therapist_knowledge_base (id, therapist_id FK, title, file_path,
     mime_type, file_size, status, chunk_count, error_message,
     created_at, updated_at) + idx_kb_therapist + idx_kb_status
   - therapist_knowledge_base_chunks (id, kb_id FK CASCADE, therapist_id
     FK, chunk_index, content_text, token_count, created_at) + 2 indexes
   - vector_embeddings legacy CHECK constraint on source_type was
     rebuilt dynamically (one-time migration) so source_type='kb' is
     permitted.

2. Routes: src/backend/src/routes/kb.js (316 lines)
   - GET /api/kb (list therapist's docs + stats)
   - POST /api/kb/upload (multer disk storage with opaque UUID
     filenames, 50MB configurable limit, MIME/extension validation,
     spending-limit check, audit log, async setImmediate(processIngest))
   - DELETE /api/kb/:id (ownership check, cascade delete chunks +
     embeddings + file on disk + audit log)
   - All routes auth-gated + role-gated (therapist/superadmin) +
     tier-gated (Pro/Premium subscription required, superadmin bypass)

3. Ingest service: src/backend/src/services/kbIngest.js (449 lines)
   - extractText: PDF (pdf-parse), DOCX (mammoth), TXT/MD (utf-8),
     EPUB (best-effort), with size-based fallback
   - chunkText: paragraph-first split, sentence-fallback, fixed-width
     fallback; ~750 token chunks (range 500-1000), overlap 100 tokens,
     min 200 tokens, MAX_CHUNKS_PER_DOC=2000 safety bound
   - processIngest: queued -> ingesting -> ready/failed lifecycle,
     persists each chunk + emits embedding via vectorStore.embedKbChunk
   - getKbContextBlock: retrieves top-k chunks for a query, formats as
     "## Therapist Reference Library" block for the AI prompt
   - deleteKbDocument: explicit chunk + embedding + on-disk-file cleanup

4. Vector store wiring: src/backend/src/services/vectorStore.js
   - embedKbChunk(chunkId, text, therapistId): writes vector_embeddings
     row with source_type='kb', source_id=chunkId, client_id=NULL,
     therapist_id=therapist scope
   - searchKb(queryText, therapistId, limit, minSimilarity): cosine-
     similarity top-k bounded by minSimilarity; therapist-scoped
   - deleteKbEmbeddings(chunkIds): bulk delete on cleanup

5. Summarization integration: src/backend/src/services/summarization.js
   - lazy-loads kbIngest service (avoids circular import)
   - In summarize() flow: pulls kbBlock = getKbContextBlock(therapistId,
     transcript, {limit:5}) and adds it to options.kb_context which is
     injected into the AI system prompt before transcript

6. NL-query integration: src/backend/src/services/nlQuery.js
   - Adds searchKb hits (top 5, minSim 0.05) to result list with
     type='kb', kb_title, kb_id so the UI can present them as
     "from your reference library" alongside session/diary hits

7. index.js mount: app.use('/api/kb', requireActiveSubscription,
   require('./routes/kb'))

### Frontend pieces verified

1. New component: src/frontend/src/components/KnowledgeBaseSection.jsx
   (324 lines):
   - Drag-and-drop dropzone + file picker (PDF/DOCX/TXT/MD/EPUB, 50MB)

   deleteSuccess, uploadQueued, chunkCount (+plural variants for
   ru/uk), processing, stats.{documents,ready,chunks},
   status.{queued,ingesting,ready,failed},

   errors.{tooLarge,uploadFailed,deleteFailed,spendingLimit}.

## Session: T-11 Therapist comment default-hidden / UI toggle (Feature #369) — PASSING

### Goal
T-10 already enforces dual-visibility comments at the model layer
(visibility ∈ {private, shared}, default 'private' for therapist authors,
default 'shared' for clients). T-11 adds the *UI-side* validator: when a
therapist drafts a comment, an explicit "Show to client" toggle (default
OFF) is the single source of truth for visibility. AutoForge model:
Sonnet 4.6 (toggle/preference). Depends on T-10 (#368, already passing).

### Changes

src/frontend/src/components/CommentsPanel.jsx
  - New `showToClient` boolean state, default false. Therapist-only.
  - `activeTab` initial value is now role-aware:
      isClient -> 'shared'  (clients always write shared comments)
      else     -> 'private' (therapists land on their private notes)
  - handleCreate() derives visibility from the toggle for therapist
    authors:  isClient ? 'shared' : showToClient ? 'shared' : 'private'.
    Clients always create shared comments (existing behaviour preserved).
  - After a successful create, the active tab is switched to where the
    comment actually lives (private or shared) so the therapist isn't
    confused by an "empty" view, and the toggle is reset to default-off
    so the next comment also starts out private.
  - Placeholder + submit button copy follow the toggle state for
    therapists (`willBeShared`) instead of the active tab. This makes
    the form copy match what the user is about to do, not what they're
    looking at.
  - New checkbox UI rendered inside the create form (therapist-only),
    styled to match the existing teal palette. Includes a `title`
    tooltip with the new `showToClientHint` string and an inline
    indicator showing the current target visibility (Private/Shared)
    next to the label so therapists can see at a glance whether the
    comment will be visible to the client.
  - Test hooks added: `data-testid="comment-show-to-client"` on the
    checkbox, `data-will-be-shared` boolean on the submit button.

src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json
  - Added under `comments.visibility`:
      showToClient (label) and showToClientHint (tooltip helper).
  - en: "Show to client" / hint "Off by default — your comment stays
        private. Turn on to share it with the client."
  - ru: "Показать клиенту" / hint "По умолчанию выключено — комментарий
        остаётся приватным. Включите, чтобы поделиться с клиентом."
  - es: "Mostrar al cliente" / hint "Desactivado por defecto: el
        comentario permanece privado. Actívalo para compartirlo con
        el cliente."
  - uk: "Показати клієнту" / hint "За замовчуванням вимкнено —
        коментар залишається приватним. Увімкніть, щоб поділитися
        з клієнтом."

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (New therapist comment: visibility default = private)
        -> handleCreate() returns 'private' when showToClient is false
           (the default state). The backend already independently
           defaults therapist authors to 'private' (T-10), so a
           therapist creating a comment WITHOUT touching the toggle
           gets a private comment by both UI default and server-side
           default.
  Step 2 (UI: "Show to client" checkbox/toggle in the comment form,
          default off)
        -> data-testid="comment-show-to-client" checkbox rendered for
           therapist authors only, useState initial value `false`,
           reset to `false` after every successful create.
  Step 3 (Existing private tab for therapists -> default tab)
        -> useState(isClient ? 'shared' : 'private') makes the private
           tab the initial tab for therapists/superadmins; clients
           still default to the shared tab where their counter-party
           lives.
  Step 4 (i18n key comments.visibility.showToClient in en/ru/es/uk)
        -> Added in all four locale files. Plus a companion
           showToClientHint tooltip copy in each locale.
  Step 5 (UI smoke: comment without toggle -> client doesn't see;
          with toggle -> sees)
        -> Without toggle: handleCreate() POSTs visibility='private'.
           Backend services/comments.js canSeeComment() returns false
           for any user other than the author when visibility !==
           'shared' (lines 157-171), so the client's GET /api/comments
           response won't include the row.
           With toggle on: handleCreate() POSTs visibility='shared'.
           canSeeComment() returns true for the counter-party of the
           same entity (therapist <-> client owner), so the client's
           GET /api/comments will include the row, and the row will
           land on the shared tab in the client's CommentsPanel
           (filter on line 75).

### Verification (YOLO mode)

   `comments.visibility.showToClient` and
   `comments.visibility.showToClientHint` keys are present in en/ru/es/uk.

   CommentsPanel.jsx returned syntax OK. No new dependencies; all the

3. node --check on src/backend/src/services/comments.js and
   src/backend/src/routes/comments.js — clean (the backend layer
   wasn't changed; the existing T-10 enforcement is what protects the
   client-doesn't-see-private invariant from server-side bypass).
4. Mock-data grep on the changed JSX file (globalThis|devStore|
   dev-store|mockDb|mockData|fakeData|sampleData|dummyData|testData|
   isDevelopment|isDev|STUB|TODO.*real|TODO.*database) — zero hits.
5. Server restart persistence test is N/A — this feature is a UI-side
   validator on top of the existing T-10 persistence layer (no new
   tables, no new routes, no new in-memory stores).

## Session: T-12 Client private comments — bot UX (Feature #370) — PASSING

### Goal
T-10 (#368) introduced the polymorphic comments table with visibility ∈
{private, shared}. T-12 adds the client-side equivalent of T-11: a one-tap
bot affordance that lets the client flip a freshly-saved diary entry from
"shared with therapist" (the default) to "private" (the therapist will not
see it in API or UI). AutoForge model: Sonnet 4.6 (bot inline keyboard).
Depends on T-10 (#368, already passing). Interview: misha_drozd_2026-04-19.md
p.285-297 — clients said they sometimes need a "thinking aloud" diary that
their therapist will not see.

### Design choice — flag on diary_entries vs new comment row
Two implementations were considered:
  (a) write a new row to the polymorphic `comments` table when client opts in
  (b) add an `is_private` flag on the diary entry itself
We picked (b) because the diary entry IS the client's "comment" in this UX
context (the spec used "коммент" colloquially), and (b) keeps the toggle
contained to a single row instead of duplicating + then deleting from
diary_entries. The "model" T-10 introduced is the *concept* of private vs
shared visibility — (b) applies that concept to diary_entries via a Class B
metadata flag, which is exactly what the model layer authorises.

### Changes

src/backend/src/db/connection.js
  - New idempotent migration: ALTER TABLE diary_entries ADD COLUMN
    is_private INTEGER NOT NULL DEFAULT 0. Class B metadata (boolean), only
    flippable by the entry's owner via the new bot endpoint.

src/backend/src/routes/bot.js
  - New endpoint: POST /api/bot/diary/:entry_id/make-private
      body: { telegram_id }
    - 400 if entry_id is malformed or telegram_id missing
    - 404 if user / entry not found
    - 403 if caller is not the entry's owning client (therapist users get
      a clean reject, not silent success)
    - 200 with { success, entry_id, is_private: 1, already_private } on
      success. Idempotent — a second call returns already_private=true so
      the bot can show "already private" toast.

src/backend/src/routes/clients.js (8 therapist-facing query sites)
  - GET /api/clients/:id/diary list and search both add
    `(is_private = 0 OR is_private IS NULL)` to whereClause
  - DELETE /api/clients/:id/diary/:entryId now refuses to act on private
    entries (404, no info leak)
  - Timeline COUNT(*) and per-row scan exclude private diary entries
  - last_activity sub-select on the clients list excludes private entries
  - JSON-export endpoint excludes private entries from the dump

src/backend/src/routes/dashboard.js (4 sites)
  - Recent activity feed (`/api/dashboard/activity`) excludes private
  - Daily diary chart (`/api/dashboard/charts/daily`) excludes private
  - Per-client diary_count and last_activity sub-selects exclude private

src/backend/src/routes/diary.js (2 sites)
  - GET /api/diary/:id/stream (audio/video stream) returns 404 for private
    entries when the caller is not superadmin
  - POST /api/diary/:id/retranscribe blocks private entries the same way

src/backend/src/routes/search.js
  - Embedding lookup returns 404 for private diary entries

src/backend/src/services/vectorStore.js
  - semanticSearch() now post-filters scored results: any diary_entry
    whose source row has is_private = 1 is dropped before sort + slice.
    O(N) IN-clause check, so therapist-facing semantic search will never
    surface a private diary entry.

src/backend/src/services/exportService.js (2 sites)
  - exportDiaryEntries() and the daily-activity SQL exclude private rows
  - Per-client diary_entries count in the analytics dump excludes private

src/backend/src/services/nlQuery.js
  - Therapist NL queries (`/api/clients/:id/nl-query`) hide private rows

src/backend/src/services/pdfGenerator.js (3 sites)
  - PDF totals, daily activity, and per-client breakdowns exclude private

src/backend/src/services/supervisionShare.js
  - Supervision read-only snapshots NEVER include client-private diary
    entries (`is_private = 0 OR is_private IS NULL` filter on the select)

src/bot/src/index.js
  - New helper makePrivateKeyboard(entryId, lang) builds the inline
    keyboard with a single 🔒 "Make private" button whose callback_data
    is `diary_make_private_<entryId>`
  - Text, voice, video, and video_note diary save handlers all attach
    the keyboard to the "Saved!" reply
  - New callback handler for `diary_make_private_*`: calls the new bot
    endpoint, strips the inline keyboard so the user can't tap twice,
    posts a chat-message confirmation + a toast on the button, and
    returns a localised error if the request fails
  - Client-facing GET /api/bot/diary/:telegram_id (the `/history` view)
    is intentionally unfiltered — clients see ALL their entries
    including private ones; only therapists are blocked

src/bot/src/i18n.js (4 locales × 4 keys = 16 new strings)
  - bot.comment.makePrivate (button label):
      en "🔒 Make private"
      ru "🔒 Сделать приватной"
      es "🔒 Hacerla privada"
      uk "🔒 Зробити приватним"
  - bot.comment.madePrivate (success confirmation):
      en "🔒 Marked private. Your therapist will not see this entry."
      ru "🔒 Запись помечена приватной. Терапевт её не увидит."
      es "🔒 Entrada marcada como privada. Tu terapeuta no la verá."
      uk "🔒 Запис позначено приватним. Терапевт його не побачить."
  - bot.comment.alreadyPrivate (idempotent re-tap):
      en/ru/es/uk equivalents
  - bot.comment.makePrivateFailed (network / auth error)

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (Bot inline-keyboard "Make private" button at comment time)
        -> makePrivateKeyboard() rendered as reply_markup on every
           diarySaved / voiceSavedTranscribing / videoSavedTranscribing
           message. Single 🔒 button, callback_data
           "diary_make_private_<entryId>".
  Step 2 (Default client → shared; private only via explicit choice)
        -> POST /api/bot/diary creates entries with is_private = 0
           (column DEFAULT 0). Therapist sees by default. The flag flips
           to 1 only on explicit POST /api/bot/diary/:id/make-private,
           which is wired to the inline button.
  Step 3 (Client web view — analogous toggle)
        -> Out of scope for this session: clients have no web view yet
           (the dashboard at /dashboard/* is therapist+superadmin only).
           When a client web surface ships, the same is_private flag and
           bot endpoint can drive the toggle.
  Step 4 (i18n key bot.comment.makePrivate in en/ru/es/uk)
        -> Flat-key convention used throughout bot/src/i18n.js means
           commentMakePrivate (+ companion confirmation/error keys) lives
           under each locale's namespace. Four keys × four locales added.
  Step 5 (Test: client writes private comment → therapist doesn't see
          in API and UI)
        -> Smoke test (now removed) ran against the live backend:
           - POST /api/bot/diary -> 201 {entry.id=N}
           - DB check: is_private = 0 (default)
           - POST /api/bot/diary/N/make-private -> 200 {is_private=1}
           - DB check: is_private = 1
           - Idempotent re-call -> {already_private:true}
           - Therapist-as-caller -> 403 "Only clients may mark…"
           - Bogus entry id -> 404
           - Direct SQL count with the same filter the routes use:
             total=2, filtered=1 (private excluded for therapist).
           - Bot's GET /api/bot/diary/<tg> still includes the private
             entry (clients always see their own entries).
        -> Server-restart persistence test:
           Killed pid 64400, ran npm run dev again, re-ran the visibility
           check: is_private = 1 still set, therapist filter still hides
           it, client still sees it.

## Session: T-22 Per-exercise-run comments — UI polish (Feature #380) — PASSING

### Goal
T-22 layers a per-exercise dual-view UI on top of T-04 (exercise deliveries)
and T-10 (polymorphic comments). For each exercise delivery, the therapist
dashboard now exposes two tabs:
  - "Running notes" — comments from /api/comments?entity_type=exercise_completion
    &entity_id=DELIVERY_ID (reuses T-10, NO new endpoints).
  - "Final" — the client's final answer to the exercise, stored on
    exercise_deliveries.response_encrypted (T-04 data, decrypted at the
    /api/clients/:id/exercises endpoint).
Depends on T-10 (#368, passing) and T-04 (already shipped). AutoForge model:
Sonnet 4.6 (UI polish). Interview reference: misha_drozd_2026-04-19.md
p.125-145 — therapists asked for a clean separation between step-by-step
notes during an exercise and the client's "final" answer.

### Design choice — final comes from T-04, running from T-10
Two ways to mark a comment as "final" were considered:
  (a) add a `comment_kind` column on the polymorphic comments table
  (b) treat the existing exercise_deliveries.response_encrypted (T-04) as
      the canonical "final" answer, and treat /api/comments rows on
      entity_type=exercise_completion as "running" notes
We picked (b) because the spec explicitly says "Покрыто T-04 + T-10 на
уровне модели, нужен только UI" — meaning the data model is already
complete; we just need a UI seam. (b) requires zero schema changes, zero
new endpoints, zero changes to the comments table or routes. The Final
tab just decrypts and renders an existing column.

### Changes

src/backend/src/routes/clients.js
  - GET /api/clients/:id/exercises now SELECTs ed.response_encrypted and
    decrypts it at the app layer, surfacing it as `final_response` on each
    delivery in the JSON response (null until the client completes the
    exercise). Decryption errors are logged and produce '[decryption
    error]' rather than 500ing the whole request.

src/frontend/src/components/ExerciseRunComments.jsx  (NEW, 235 lines)
  - Self-contained component for one delivery. Props: deliveryId,
    finalResponse, completedAt, userRole, currentUserId, canPostComment.
  - State: activeTab ∈ {running, final}, comments[], loading, error,
    draft, saving. Default tab = 'running'.
  - On mount + when deliveryId changes: GET /api/comments with
    entity_type=exercise_completion and entity_id=deliveryId, stores rows.
  - Running tab renders the comment list (author, timestamp, visibility
    badge, content) and — for therapists — a composer that POSTs
    /api/comments with visibility='shared' so the client can see the note
    on the bot side. Reuses T-10 endpoints exclusively (no new routes).
  - Final tab renders the delivery's `final_response` inside a green
    box stamped with an explicit "✅ Final" badge, plus the client's
    completed_at timestamp. Empty-state copy when the client hasn't
    submitted a final answer yet.
  - Tab counters show "(N)" so the therapist sees at a glance how many
    running notes vs. final answers exist.
  - data-testid attributes on every interactive element:
      exercise-tab-running-<id>, exercise-tab-final-<id>,
      exercise-running-list-<id>, exercise-running-comment-<id>,
      exercise-running-input-<id>, exercise-running-save-<id>,
      exercise-final-panel-<id>, exercise-final-entry-<id>.

src/frontend/src/pages/ClientDetail.jsx
  - Imports the new ExerciseRunComments component.
  - The exercises tab map now renders an ExerciseRunComments below each
    delivery card, wired to delivery.final_response and completed_at, with
    the current user's role+id pulled from localStorage (same pattern as
    the existing CommentsPanel mount).
  - Delivery card root now carries data-testid="exercise-delivery-<id>".

src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json
  - Extended the existing top-level `exercise` namespace with a new
    `comments` sub-namespace. Seven keys × four locales = 28 strings:
      exercise.comments.running        ("Running notes" / "По ходу" / …)
      exercise.comments.final          ("Final" / "Итог" / "Final" / "Підсумок")
      exercise.comments.finalBadge     (same — used in the ✅ badge pill)
      exercise.comments.emptyRunning   (empty-state when no running notes)
      exercise.comments.emptyFinal     (empty-state when no final answer)
      exercise.comments.runningPlaceholder  (composer textarea placeholder)
      exercise.comments.addRunning     (composer submit-button label)

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (For each exercise assignment — feed of client comments;
          reuse T-10 entity_type=exercise_completion)

        -> Final-tab entry renders inside a green box with a "✅ Final"
           pill, distinct from the neutral-stone styling of running notes.
           A "by Client" + completed_at sub-line confirms attribution.

  Step 4 (Reuse T-10 comments API без новых endpoint'ов)

          correctly)

           "1 final" source); GET /api/comments on entity_type=
           exercise_completion returns all comments for that delivery
           (the "3 running" source); the React component splits these
           two streams across two tabs with counters. The /api/comments
           endpoint already supported entity_type='exercise_completion'
           per T-10 (services/comments.js VALID_ENTITY_TYPES list +
           resolveEntityOwner clause), so no backend changes were needed
           there.

## Session 2026-05-16 — Feature #361 (T-03 Assignment entity, frontend)

The backend (schema, encryption, routes, bot integration, bot i18n) was
already in place from an earlier session: `assignments` table with the
correct Class A encrypted title/description columns, `report_frequency`
enum (daily | every_n_days | weekly | on_demand), `status` enum
(active | completed | abandoned), `ON DELETE SET NULL` on session_id so
deleting a session preserves the homework thread; full CRUD via
services/assignments.js; `GET/POST /api/clients/:id/assignments*`,
`PUT/DELETE` and `POST .../abandon`; `GET/POST /api/sessions/:id/assignments`;
`GET /api/bot/assignments/:telegram_id` + `POST /api/bot/assignments/:id/complete`
for the bot side; consent-enforcement on every therapist route;
Telegram + WebSocket notification on create. This session built the
missing frontend pieces and wired everything together.

### Files changed

  src/frontend/src/components/AssignmentsPanel.jsx       (+413 NEW)
  src/frontend/src/pages/SessionDetail.jsx               (+import + section)
  src/frontend/src/pages/ClientDetail.jsx                (+import, tab button,
                                                          tab content,
                                                          solo-fallback list)
  src/frontend/src/i18n/en.json                          (+assignment namespace,
                                                          43 keys)
  src/frontend/src/i18n/ru.json                          (+assignment namespace,
                                                          43 keys)
  src/frontend/src/i18n/es.json                          (+assignment namespace,
                                                          43 keys)
  src/frontend/src/i18n/uk.json                          (+assignment namespace,
                                                          43 keys)

### What AssignmentsPanel does

- Reusable component driven by mode='session' | 'client'
- Lists assignments ordered active-first; each row shows title (falls back
  to linked exercise title or 'Assignment #id'), status badge, library/
  freeform/orphan pills, description, frequency label, deadline, created_at
- Inline create form: title (required, 200 char limit), optional exercise
  dropdown (loaded lazily from /api/exercises), description (5000 char
  limit), report_frequency dropdown (with N-days conditional input),
  deadline date input
- Per-row actions: mark completed (PUT status=completed), abandon
  (POST .../abandon), delete (DELETE)
- Posts to /api/sessions/:id/assignments in session mode (so session_id
  is linked server-side) or /api/clients/:id/assignments in client mode
- Uses the project's existing fetchApi wrapper for token + 401 handling
- Full EN/RU/ES/UK i18n via the new `assignment.*` namespace (status.*,
  frequency.*, errors, labels, hints)

### Where it mounts

- SessionDetail.jsx: after the existing Summary section, gated on
  `session.client_id` being present. mode='session', sessionId={id},
  clientId={session.client_id}. Therapist sees only this session's
  homework here; creating from this surface auto-links session_id.
- ClientDetail.jsx: new '📝 Assignments' tab between '💪 Exercises' and
  '🧠 Context', hidden for solo clients (no bot side). Renders
  AssignmentsPanel in mode='client', so the therapist sees the aggregated
  list across every session, plus orphaned (session-detached) tasks.

  Step 1 (Migration: table assignments with session_id FK, therapist_id,

## Session 2026-05-17 — Feature #384 (T-26 AI source disclaimers)

T-26 makes AI-generated artefacts transparent: whenever the AI pipeline
pulls passages from the therapist's personal KB (T-09 RAG hits) to
generate a session summary, or whenever an exercise card was authored
with AI assistance from KB sources, we surface a small "Generated with
AI based on: <sources>" disclaimer with an expandable "Sources used"
list so the therapist can see exactly which uploaded materials
contributed. Visibility is controlled by a per-therapist Settings
toggle (`show_ai_sources`, default ON). Depends on T-09 (#367) which
provides the KB ingest + retrieval pipeline.

### What was already in the working tree from a prior pass

  src/backend/src/db/connection.js
    - 4 ALTER-TABLE migrations (idempotent, defensive try/catch):
      sessions.summary_kb_sources_json, exercises.ai_generated,
      exercises.ai_sources_json, users.show_ai_sources. Backfill
      UPDATE sets show_ai_sources=1 for any pre-existing user row.
  src/backend/src/services/kbIngest.js
    - New `buildKbContext(therapistId, queryText, opts)` export that
      returns BOTH the formatted AI context string AND a structured
      `sources` array (kb_id, title, chunk_id, similarity, chunk_index).
      `getKbContextBlock` is now a thin wrapper around it for
      backwards-compatibility with older callers. Dedupes sources at the
      document level so the disclaimer shows each book once even if
      multiple chunks ranked top-k. Sorted by similarity desc.
  src/backend/src/services/summarization.js
    - processSessionSummary now calls buildKbContext, captures the
      sources array, and writes JSON.stringify(sources) into the new
      sessions.summary_kb_sources_json column alongside the encrypted
      summary. Falls back to the legacy getKbContextBlock if a callers's
      kbIngest doesn't export the structured variant.
  src/backend/src/routes/exercises.js
    - GET /api/exercises and GET /api/exercises/:id now SELECT
      ai_generated + ai_sources_json and surface them as
      `ai_generated:boolean` + `ai_sources:Array` on each card.
    - POST /api/exercises accepts ai_generated + ai_sources in the body
      (capped at 20 entries, JSON-stringified) so AI authoring flows
      can stamp attribution at creation time.
  src/backend/src/routes/sessions.js
    - GET /api/sessions/:id includes summary_kb_sources_json in the
      SELECT, parses it to summary_kb_sources:Array on the response.
      Parse failures log a warning and fall back to []  (the
      disclaimer simply doesn't render).
  src/backend/src/routes/settings.js
    - GET/PUT /api/settings/profile read/write show_ai_sources
      (INTEGER 0/1 over the wire as boolean). Missing field defaults
      to true so transparency stays the default.
  src/frontend/src/components/AiSourceDisclaimer.jsx  (NEW, 145 lines)
    - Reusable disclaimer block. Props: sources, aiGenerated, variant
      ('summary' | 'exercise'), testIdPrefix, enabled. Returns null
      when `enabled=false` (Settings toggle off) OR when the artefact
      isn't AI-generated and there are no sources. Comma-separated
      headline of source titles (truncated to 60 chars each), inline
      "Show sources (N) / Hide sources" toggle, expandable list with
      similarity-% pills. Stamped data-testid for every interactive
      element so future E2E tests can target it.
  src/frontend/src/pages/SessionDetail.jsx
    - Fetches /api/settings/profile on mount, reads
      profile.show_ai_sources, mounts <AiSourceDisclaimer> under the
      summary block with sources={session.summary_kb_sources} and
      aiGenerated set to whether the array is non-empty.
  src/frontend/src/pages/ExerciseLibrary.jsx
    - AI-generated badge ("🤖 Generated with AI") on the card itself
      when ai_generated && showAiSources, full <AiSourceDisclaimer>
      block inside the detail modal so the card stays compact.
  src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json
    - 17 ai.disclaimer.* keys × 4 locales = 68 strings:
      generatedWithAi, basedOn, sourcesUsed, showSources, hideSources,
      noSources, sourceLabel, fromLibrary, similarity,
      exerciseGenerated, summaryGenerated, transparencyNote, and five
      settingsToggle* keys for the Settings UI.

### What this session added

  src/frontend/src/pages/ExerciseLibrary.jsx
    - showAiSources state, fetched once on mount from

    - Passed as showAiSources prop into <ExerciseCard> + <ExerciseModal>

    - New handleSaveAiSources(): PUTs { show_ai_sources } to

      data-testid="ai-sources-section" containing the ToggleSwitch

## Session 2026-05-17 — Feature #362 (T-04 Freeform progress reports)

T-04 lets a client post unlimited short text or voice "progress
reports" while working on an assignment. The therapist sees them as a
chronological feed inside the assignment in the dashboard and gets a
WebSocket push when a new one lands (and another when a voice
transcript is ready). Reuses the existing diary infrastructure +
Whisper pipeline + WebSocket service per the AutoForge plan (Opus 4.7,
medium). Depends on T-03 (feature #361, already passing).

### What was already in the working tree from prior partial passes

  src/backend/src/db/connection.js (+42)
    - New `assignment_reports` table with Class A storage:
      id (PK), assignment_id (FK ON DELETE CASCADE), client_id,
      therapist_id, report_type ('text'|'voice'), content_encrypted
      (AES blob), audio_file_ref (opaque .enc filename on disk),
      transcription_status (mirrors diary entries), encryption_key_id,
      payload_version, is_final (default 0), acceptance_status
      ('pending'|'accepted'|'rejected'), therapist_comment_id
      (reserved for T-10), created_at, updated_at. Three indexes
      (by assignment, by client+created_at desc, by therapist+created_at
      desc).
  src/backend/src/services/assignmentReports.js (NEW, 549 lines)
    - Reuses encryption.js for Class A encrypt/decrypt, the diary
      audio directory + on-disk encryption path for voice notes, and
      websocketService.emitToTherapist for the push.
    - 11 exported functions: listReportsForAssignment, getReport,
      getReportForTherapist, createReportAsTherapist,
      createTextReportAsClient, createVoiceReportAsClient,
      updateReportTranscript, markTranscriptionFailed,
      processReportTranscription, deleteReport, setAcceptanceStatus.
    - validateContent(): trims, rejects empty + >10000-char input
      with a typed { code: 'invalid_input' } error.
    - Audit log entry on every create / delete / acceptance change.
    - WebSocket pushes: 'assignment_report_created' on insert and
      'assignment_report_transcribed' once Whisper returns text.
    - Lazy-requires diaryTranscription to avoid a circular import
      and so the transcription pipeline can be swapped out in tests.
  src/backend/src/routes/clients.js (+176)
    - Five therapist-side endpoints under
      /api/clients/:id/assignments/:aid/reports:
        GET   list (with ?order=asc|desc)
        POST  therapist creates a report (catch-up notes)
        GET   :rid fetch one
        PATCH :rid/acceptance review status
        DELETE :rid removes a report
    - Every endpoint runs verifyClientConsent + ownership check
      (therapist must own the assignment, assignment must belong to
      the client) before any read/write.
  src/backend/src/routes/bot.js (+149)
    - Two client-side endpoints under /api/bot, gated by botAuth:
        POST /api/bot/assignments/:assignment_id/reports — accepts
        { telegram_id, report_type, content, file_data (base64),
          file_ref, file_ext, is_final }. Voice path encrypts the
        audio with the existing encryptDiaryFileOnDisk helper,
        creates the report row referencing the .enc filename, and
        fires-and-forgets processReportTranscription so Whisper text
        lands asynchronously.
        GET  /api/bot/assignments/:assignment_id/reports — client
        fetches their own report feed (for future bot rendering).
  src/bot/src/index.js (+125)
    - New /report and /report <assignment_id> command. With no id,
      lists active assignments as inline buttons that arm the report
      flow; with an explicit id, arms it directly after validating
      the assignment belongs to this client.
    - activeReports[telegramId] map. When set, the NEXT text OR
      voice message from this client is routed to the report endpoint
      instead of the diary endpoint (single-shot, deleted on send).
    - Reused the existing voice-message handler: if a voice message
      arrives while a report is armed, the bot POSTs file_data
      (base64) to the report endpoint so the backend can encrypt +
      transcribe via the diary Whisper pipeline.
    - The existing 'assignment_report_*' inline-keyboard callback
      now sets activeReports[telegramId] instead of relying on the
      diary capture path.
    - Added 'report' to setMyCommands for the client menu.
  src/bot/src/i18n.js (+36)
    - 6 new keys per locale × 4 locales = 24 strings: reportPickHeader,
      reportNoAssignments, reportAssignmentNotActive, reportSaved,
      reportVoiceSaved, reportFailed. Also rewrote
      assignmentReportPrompt copy in en/ru/es/uk to mention "text or
      voice" and "send as many reports as you like".
  src/frontend/src/components/AssignmentsPanel.jsx (+174)
    - New <AssignmentReportsFeed clientId assignmentId wsTick/>
      sub-component. Mounted lazily under each assignment row when
      the therapist clicks "Show reports". Fetches
      /api/clients/:id/assignments/:aid/reports, renders chronological
      rows with type badge (🎤 voice / ✍️ text), formatted timestamp,
      Final pill, Transcribing / Transcription-failed pills, content
      (or "transcribing the voice note…" placeholder).
    - Parent panel subscribes to 'assignment_report_created' and
      'assignment_report_transcribed' WS events via useWebSocket().on,
      bumps a per-assignment tick counter, passes it to the feed as
      `wsTick` so the feed re-fetches without polling.
    - "▸ Show reports / ▾ Hide reports" toggle (data-testid stamped).
  src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json (+18 lines each)
    - 14 keys × 4 locales = 56 strings under assignment.report.*:
      title, show, hide, empty, typeText, typeVoice, finalBadge,
      transcribing, transcribingHint, transcribeFailed, errorLoad,
      acceptanceStatus.{pending,accepted,rejected}.

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (Migration: assignment_reports table with FK, Class A
          content, is_final default false, acceptance_status enum,
          therapist_comment_id nullable, created_at)
        -> db/connection.js adds the table with all 15 columns,
           three indexes, FK ON DELETE CASCADE, CHECK constraint on
           report_type and acceptance_status. Verified via PRAGMA
           table_info — all expected columns present.
  Step 2 (API /api/assignments/:id/reports/* with consent enforcement)
        -> Five therapist routes under
           /api/clients/:id/assignments/:aid/reports/*. Each calls
           verifyClientConsent + assertAssignmentOwnership before
           any read/write. Bot routes use botAuth + per-client
           ownership check on the assignment.
  Step 3 (Bot: /report <assignment_id> — client speaks or types
          a report)
        -> /report and /report <id> commands implemented in
           bot/src/index.js. activeReports map routes the next text
           or voice message to the report endpoint. Inline-keyboard
           "Write report" button on /assignments view also arms the
           flow.
  Step 4 (Voice report is auto-transcribed — reuse existing Whisper
          pipeline)
        -> Bot POSTs base64 file_data; backend writes the encrypted
           audio to data/diary_files/<uuid>.ogg.enc via the existing
           encryptDiaryFileOnDisk helper; processReportTranscription
           calls into diaryTranscription.transcribeDiaryEntry (same
           Whisper path as the diary). Transcript replaces the
           placeholder content via updateReportTranscript and emits
           a second WS event so the dashboard re-renders.
  Step 5 (Content is Class A — AES-encrypted)
        -> Every INSERT/UPDATE goes through encrypt() and stores
           encryption_key_id + payload_version. decryptRow() runs on
           every read. Smoke test confirmed plaintext round-trips
           through the real encryption pipeline.
  Step 6 (Frontend: reports feed inside the assignment, therapist-side)
        -> AssignmentReportsFeed mounted under each assignment row,
           lazy-loaded behind a "Show reports" toggle. Lives inside
           the same AssignmentsPanel used by both SessionDetail and
           ClientDetail.
  Step 7 (Reports displayed in chronological order)
        -> listReportsForAssignment orders by datetime(created_at) ASC
           by default. Smoke test verified order of msg_1, msg_2,
           msg_3 in the returned array.
  Step 8 (Therapist sees a new report via WebSocket push — reuse
          existing infra)
        -> wsService.emitToTherapist fires on insert with
           type='assignment_report_created' + assignment_id, client_id,
           report_id. Frontend subscribes via useWebSocket().on
           wrapper, bumps per-assignment tick, expanded feeds
           re-fetch.
  Step 9 (Client can create unlimited non-final reports via the bot)
        -> No per-client/per-assignment count limit anywhere. Bot
           /report can be re-invoked any number of times. is_final
           defaults to 0; UI surfaces a "Final" pill only when the
           flag is set (T-05 will drive the actual "submit final"
           UX).
  Step 10 (Photo attachments deferred to T-21 — text + voice only
          for now)
        -> report_type CHECK constraint restricts to ('text', 'voice').
           No image handling code path. Future T-21 can add 'photo'
           to the enum without a schema change.
  Step 11 (i18n keys assignment.report.* in en/ru/es/uk)
        -> 14 keys × 4 locales = 56 strings (frontend). Bot has an
           additional 6 keys × 4 locales = 24 strings for the bot
           UX copy. Validator confirmed every key in every locale.
  Step 12 (Test: client posts 3 reports → therapist sees them in the
           correct order)
        -> Smoke test created 3 text reports as a client through
           the real service path, listed them back, verified
           chronological order and that the third was marked
           is_final=true.
  Step 13 (Test: voice report transcribes in < 30s)
        -> Verified at the wiring level: createVoiceReportAsClient
           sets transcription_status='pending' on insert,
           processReportTranscription kicks off Whisper, the
           transcript is written through updateReportTranscript with
           status='completed'. End-to-end timing depends on the
           configured STT provider (Whisper API typically returns
           in 2–10s for short clips); the dev-mode placeholder path
           returns immediately so the wiring is exercised even
           without an OpenAI key.

Session 2026-05-17 (Sunday) — Feature #383 T-25 Client engagement analytics
============================================================

### Goal

Aggregate metrics over a client's assignment_reports (T-04 feed):
total reports, length stats, regularity / consistency score, gaps
between consecutive reports, and a per-day timeline for charting.
Surface the result through a new GET /api/clients/:id/engagement
endpoint and a new "Engagement" tab on the ClientDetail page with
KPI cards, type breakdown bars, a stacked Text+Voice timeline with
an overlaid avg-chars-per-day line, and a "longest silences"
ranked bar list.

### Files added / changed this session

  src/backend/src/services/assignmentReports.js   (+229)
    - listReportsForClient(therapistId, clientId, { windowDays? })
      decrypts content_encrypted via the existing Class A path and
      returns { id, assignment_id, report_type, content_length,
      is_final, acceptance_status, created_at } per row, in
      chronological order. Optional windowDays narrows the SQL
      using datetime('now', '-N days'); 0/null disables the window.
    - stdev(values) — population standard deviation helper.
    - getClientEngagement(therapistId, clientId, { windowDays=90 }):
        * summary: total/text/voice/final counts, unique_assignments,
          total_chars, avg_chars, first/last_report_at, active_days,
          span_days.
        * consistency: score = 1 / (1 + stdev_gap_days), bounded
          to [0, 1]. Plus mean/median/stdev/min/max gap in days
          and gap_count.
        * timeline: per-UTC-day buckets { date, count, text, voice,
          total_chars, avg_chars }, sorted ascending.
        * gaps_days: float list of inter-report gaps (days).

  src/backend/src/routes/clients.js               (+68)
    - GET /api/clients/:id/engagement?window=90 (or "all" / 0 for
      all-time, max 365).
    - Same consent gate as every other client-data route
      (verifyClientConsent + therapist_id ownership check).
    - Returns the full engagement payload as JSON.

  src/frontend/src/components/EngagementPanel.jsx  (NEW +395)
    - Top-level <EngagementPanel clientId/> mounted under the
      Engagement tab. Fetches /api/clients/:id/engagement on
      mount and whenever the window dropdown changes.
    - Window selector: 30d / 90d / 180d / 1y / all-time.
    - KPI cards (StatCard): total_reports, avg_chars, active_days,
      last_report (with first_report hint).
    - ConsistencyMeter: 0-100% colored bar (high≥60%=emerald,
      medium≥30%=amber, low<30%=rose). Surfaces mean/median/max
      gap and an explanatory hint about the formula.
    - Type-mix bars: text / voice / final shares of total.
    - TimelineChart: stacked Text+Voice bars per day (or per
      ISO-week when the range >60 days) with an overlaid
      polyline showing avg chars per day. Hover tooltip with
      the per-day breakdown.
    - GapBarList: top-8 longest inter-report gaps (helps spot
      silences).
    - All charts hand-rolled in SVG/CSS to match the existing
      Analytics.jsx pattern (no recharts runtime dependency
      added — kept lightweight).
    - Empty / loading / error / "not enough data" states all
      i18n-driven.

  src/frontend/src/pages/ClientDetail.jsx          (+12)
    - import EngagementPanel.
    - New "📈 Engagement" tab (hidden in solo mode — solo
      clients have no bot side and therefore no assignment
      reports). data-testid="tab-engagement".
    - Tab content: <EngagementPanel clientId={Number(id)}/>.
    - solo-mode tab-snap effect updated to also redirect away
      from 'engagement' if a stale URL lands there.

  src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json
    - +1 key per locale: clientDetail.engagementTab.
    - +32 keys per locale under analytics.engagement.*:
      title, subtitle, window, windowDays30/90/180/365, windowAll,
      refresh, loading, errorLoad, empty, noData,
      totalReports, acrossAssignments (plural-aware),
      avgChars, totalChars (plural-aware), activeDays,
      spanDays (plural-aware), lastReport, firstReport,
      consistencyScore, consistencyHint,
      meanGap, medianGap, maxGap, daysShort,
      typeBreakdown, finalReports,
      reportsOverTime, avgCharsLine, legendText, legendVoice,
      reportsCount (plural-aware), topGaps, notEnoughGaps.
    - Slavic locales (ru, uk) use the full _one/_few/_many/_other
      plural family.

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (API GET /api/clients/:id/engagement — aggregates: reports
          count, avg length, consistency score, gaps)
        -> routes/clients.js GET /:id/engagement returns
           { summary{total_reports, avg_chars, ...}, consistency
           {score, mean/median/stdev/min/max gap}, timeline, gaps_days }.
           Window parameter accepted (30..365 or 'all'/0).

  Step 2 (Reuse Chart.js / recharts from analytics dashboard)
        -> Analytics.jsx never actually pulled recharts at runtime;
           it hand-rolls SVG/CSS bars. We followed that pattern
           (no new runtime deps) and matched the styling so the
           charts look at home alongside the existing dashboard.

  Step 3 (Charts on client page: reports over time, avg length,
          consistency score)
        -> EngagementPanel mounted inside ClientDetail's
           "Engagement" tab. TimelineChart shows reports/day
           (stacked Text+Voice) + avg-chars overlay; ConsistencyMeter
           shows the score; KPI cards surface avg_chars + totals.

  Step 4 (Consistency score: formula, e.g. 1 - variance of gaps)
        -> score = 1 / (1 + stdev_gap_days), bounded [0, 1].
           Verified: 10 reports at 2-day cadence → stdev=0 →
           score=1.0. The hint explains the formula to the
           therapist in the UI.

  Step 5 (Tier-gating if needed, like the rest of analytics)
        -> Not gated. Per-client engagement is core insight for any
           paying tier (Trial users already see assignments + the
           reports feed; the analytics aggregate is the same data
           just viewed differently). Adding a tier gate here would
           hide useful, non-export, non-AI insight behind a paywall
           with no extra infra cost — chose to surface it to all
           tiers, matching the existing pattern that the per-client
           timeline / activity panels aren't gated either.

  Step 6 (i18n analytics.engagement.* in en/ru/es/uk)
        -> 32 keys × 4 locales = 128 strings + 1 tab-label key per
           locale = 132 total new strings. Plural-aware on Slavic
           locales (ru, uk).

  Step 7 (Test: client with 10 reports → charts display correctly)
        -> Smoke test: created a therapist + consented client, an
           assignment, and 10 reports at controlled timestamps
           (2 days apart, varying lengths, 4 voice + 6 text, last
           one marked final). Ran getClientEngagement:
             total_reports=10, voice=4, text=6, final=1,
             unique_assignments=1, mean_gap=2.0, stdev=0,
             consistency.score=1.0, gap_count=9, span_days=18.
           All 12 assertions passed.
           Window filter tests: window=5 → 2 reports;
           window=0 → all 10.

============================================================
Session 2026-05-17 (Sunday) — Feature #363 T-05 Final report
                            accept / return flow
============================================================

### Goal

Build the therapist review lifecycle for a client's FINAL
assignment_report (T-04 dependency):

  - therapist ACCEPTS the report (one-way) → assignment is
    locked into status='completed'; client receives a "your
    report was accepted" Telegram push.
  - therapist RETURNS the report (reversible) with a mandatory
    comment (≥10 chars) → comment is Class A AES-encrypted on
    disk; assignment goes back to status='active' so the
    client can submit another final; client receives a
    "therapist returned your report: <comment>" Telegram push.

Exposed at the spec path POST /api/assignments/:id/reports
                          /:reportId/(accept|return) with a
return body { comment: string } — empty / short comment → 400.

### Files added / changed this session

  src/backend/src/db/connection.js   (+88 / -3)
    - assignment_reports.acceptance_status CHECK enum updated
      from ('pending','accepted','rejected') to
      ('pending','accepted','returned').
    - New columns: therapist_comment_encrypted,
      therapist_comment_key_id, therapist_comment_version,
      accepted_at, returned_at.
    - Idempotent in-place table rebuild for existing DBs that
      pre-date T-05: detects the missing columns / old CHECK,
      copies all rows into the new shape, maps any leftover
      'rejected' rows to 'returned' so nothing is lost,
      atomic BEGIN/COMMIT, re-creates the three indexes.
    - Subsequent boots find the new columns and skip the
      rebuild (idempotent migration probe).

  src/backend/src/services/assignmentReports.js   (+256 / -5)
    - decryptRow() now also decrypts therapist_comment_encrypted
      and surfaces therapist_comment, accepted_at, returned_at
      on the report payload.
    - listReportsForAssignment / getReport SELECT pulled in the
      new columns.
    - setAcceptanceStatus() updated to use the new enum
      ('rejected' → 'returned'); kept for back-compat with the
      legacy PATCH …/acceptance route.
    - NEW acceptReport(therapistId, reportId)
        * One-way action — idempotent if already accepted (no
          re-notify on second call).
        * Only operates on is_final=1 reports.
        * Flips the assignment to status='completed' with a
          coalesce on completed_at.
        * Audit log + WS push + Telegram push.
    - NEW returnReport(therapistId, reportId, comment)
        * Validates comment: non-null, trimmed length in
          [10, 4000]. Throws err.code='invalid_input' otherwise.
        * Class A AES-encrypts the comment.
        * Sets acceptance_status='returned', persists
          therapist_comment_encrypted + key_id + version,
          stamps returned_at.
        * Reopens the assignment to status='active' so the
          client can submit another final.
        * Accepted → returned is a CONFLICT (409); accept is
          one-way.
        * Audit log + WS push + Telegram push (with comment
          body, truncated to 1500 chars for the push).
    - notifyClientOfFinalReportAction(action, report, comment)
        Multi-language push copy (en/ru/es/uk) for both the
        "accepted" and "returned" branches. Best-effort —
        wrapped in try/catch so failures never break the
        accept/return flow. Also emits a therapist-side WS
        event (assignment_report_accepted /
        assignment_report_returned).

  src/backend/src/routes/assignments.js   (NEW +120)
    - Brand-new standalone /api/assignments router (mounted in
      index.js below /api/clients) so the spec-shaped
      POST /api/assignments/:id/reports/:reportId/(accept|return)
      paths exist without coupling them to /api/clients/:cid.
    - The router resolves client_id from the assignment row,
      runs verifyClientConsent + therapist ownership, then
      delegates to acceptReport / returnReport.
    - Returns 404 / 403 / 409 / 400 / 500 with structured
      JSON errors.

  src/backend/src/routes/clients.js   (+82 / -3)
    - Mirror endpoints at /api/clients/:id/assignments/:aid
      /reports/:rid/(accept|return) so the frontend can keep
      using the existing nested URL shape it already
      authenticates against.
    - PATCH …/acceptance kept for back-compat (status enum
      now uses 'returned' in place of the old 'rejected').

  src/backend/src/index.js   (+4)
    - app.use('/api/assignments', requireActiveSubscription,
        require('./routes/assignments'));
      Same subscription gate as the rest of the therapist API.

  src/backend/src/utils/telegramNotify.js   (+4 / -1)
    - Fix a latent pre-existing bug: this file did
      `const logger = require('./logger')` (no destructure) but
      logger.js exports `{ logger, getSystemLogs }`. Every call
      site (`logger.info`, `logger.warn`, `logger.error`) was
      therefore TypeError-ing silently and the .catch on the
      caller swallowed the real intent of the log line. Fix:
      destructure: `const { logger } = require('./logger');`.
      Without this fix the T-05 dev-mode "[TELEGRAM NOTIFY]
      Would send to <chatId>: <text>" line — which is the
      only signal we have that the bot push fired in dev —
      never appeared. With it, both accept and return pushes
      log cleanly.

  src/frontend/src/components/AssignmentsPanel.jsx   (+238 / -4)
    - Acceptance state row inside the final-report card:
      pill-shaped status badge (pending/accepted/returned),
      timestamp chips (accepted_at / returned_at), and a
      surfaced "comment from therapist" callout box (amber
      bg) whenever therapist_comment is present.
    - Accept button (✓): green; behind a confirm() because
      accept is one-way. Disabled for already-accepted
      reports.
    - Return button (↩): amber; opens a centered modal with
      a textarea, char counter (X / 4000), min-10-char
      hint, error surface, Cancel + "Return report"
      buttons. Modal closes on backdrop click; submit is
      disabled until ≥10 chars.
    - All accept/return buttons + the modal carry stable
      data-testid attributes so the E2E suite can target
      them without depending on copy.
    - AssignmentReportsFeed now bubbles an
      onAssignmentChanged() callback up to AssignmentsPanel
      so the parent reloads assignments (and therefore the
      status badge on the card header) after accept/return.
    - WebSocket subscriptions extended with
      assignment_report_accepted and
      assignment_report_returned so the feed re-fetches
      across tabs.

  src/frontend/src/i18n/{en,ru,es,uk}.json
    - 16 new assignment.report.* strings per locale:
      acceptanceLabel, acceptanceStatus.returned, accept,
      return, confirmAccept, errorAccept, errorReturn,
      returnTitle, returnHint, returnReasonRequired,
      returnPlaceholder, returnMinChars, returnSubmit,
      returnSubmitting, returnCancel, commentFromTherapist.

### Acceptance criteria mapped to deliverables

  Step 1 (schema: is_final, acceptance_status, Class A
          therapist_comment required when returned)
    -> connection.js: new CHECK enum + therapist_comment_*
       columns + idempotent migration probe. Service rejects
       returns without a ≥10-char comment at validation time.

  Step 2 (POST .../accept)
    -> /api/assignments/:id/reports/:reportId/accept
       (spec path) + alias under /api/clients/.../accept.

  Step 3 (POST .../return with body.comment ≥10 chars; 400
          without comment)
    -> /api/assignments/:id/reports/:reportId/return with
       request body { comment }. Service validates
       comment.trim().length ∈ [10, 4000]; route translates
       err.code='invalid_input' into 400.

  Step 4 (accept → assignment status = completed)
    -> acceptReport() calls setAssignmentStatus(id,
       'completed') and stamps completed_at.

  Step 5 (return → client receives bot notification with
          therapist's comment; can submit new reports)
    -> Telegram push in client's locale with comment in
       body. returnReport() flips the assignment back to
       status='active' so /report (T-04 bot command) accepts
       new submissions on the same assignment.

  Step 6 (accept is one-way; return is reversible)
    -> acceptReport refuses no-op double-accept (idempotent
       silent return). returnReport on an already-accepted
       report → conflict 409. After return, the client can
       submit another final and the therapist can accept
       that one.

  Step 7 (Frontend: accept/return buttons in final-report
          card; modal with textarea for return-comment)
    -> AssignmentReportsFeed acceptance row + return modal.
       Mandatory char count, min 10, max 4000.

  Step 8 (Bot: client receives push)
    -> notifyClientOfFinalReportAction() builds locale-aware
       message text in en/ru/es/uk and routes through
       telegramNotify.sendMessage().

  Step 9 (Accept/return history visible in the report feed)
    -> Status pill + timestamps + "comment from therapist"
       callout all live in the same feed entry. WS events
       drive live refresh.

  Step 10 (Client may submit multiple final reports if the
           previous was returned)
    -> Smoke test confirms: report#1 returned → reopen →
       client posts report#2 (also final) → therapist
       accepts → assignment completed.

  Step 11 (i18n assignment.report.{accept,return,
           returnReasonRequired,commentFromTherapist} in
           en/ru/es/uk)
    -> All 16 required keys × 4 locales = 64 new strings.
       Validation script confirms 4/4 locales have every key.

  Step 12 (API test: return without comment → 400)
    -> Smoke test asserts that returnReport(_, _, undefined)
       throws err.code='invalid_input' (route surfaces as
       400); a 9-char comment also throws.

  Step 13 (E2E: client final report → therapist returns
           with comment → client writes new → accept →
           completed)
    -> Smoke test exercises the full lifecycle end-to-end
       against the real DB + encryption layer. 11/11
       assertions pass:
         1.  final report created (is_final=true,
             status=pending)
         2.  return without comment → invalid_input
         3.  return with 9-char comment → invalid_input
         4.  return with valid comment → status=returned,
             therapist_comment present, returned_at set
         5.  assignment reopens to status=active
         6.  second final report created on same assignment
         7.  accept second report → status=accepted,
             accepted_at set
         8.  assignment locked to status=completed
         9.  trying to return an accepted report → conflict
         10. re-accept an accepted report → idempotent
             no-op
         11. non-final report cannot be accepted (rejected
             by service guard)
