## Session 2026-05-17 21:00 — Feature #385: QA bug sweep of recent merges (T-04, T-05, T-21, T-25, T-26)

### Scope
Cross-file audit of the last 5 merges in `dev`:
  - 12ca16c  T-05  final report accept and return flow
  - 476e732  T-25  client engagement analytics (#383)
  - 11dac9d  T-21  photo attachments on assignment reports (#379)
  - 0ac1f74  T-04  freeform progress reports per assignment (#362)
  - de30d0a  T-26  AI source disclaimers (#384)

Shared touch points: services/assignmentReports.js, routes/clients.js,
db/connection.js, components/AssignmentsPanel.jsx, bot/index.js — high
interference risk. Read each merge's full diff against the current `dev`
HEAD state and stepped through every concern called out in feature #385's
verification steps.

### Audit conclusions per feature

**T-04 (freeform progress reports)**
- activeReports[telegramId] race:
  * Voice handler (bot/index.js:1765) and text handler (:2287) both check
    AND delete the entry → second message correctly falls through to diary.
  * Photo handler (:1977) intentionally does NOT delete the entry so a
    text/voice follow-up can attach to the same parent report. By design.
  * No TTL on activeReports — stale entries persist until next /report or
    bot restart. Minor; not a leak. Filed as a future polish item only.
- Ownership chain:
  * /api/clients/.../reports/* routes all run through verifyClientConsent
    + assertAssignmentOwnership (which calls assignmentsService.getAssignment
    scoped to therapist+client+assignment).
  * The accept/return alias router at /api/assignments/:id/reports/:rid/...
    additionally re-checks ownership via findAssignmentBase. Belt+braces.
  * Voice transcription is fired as `processReportTranscription(report.id)
    .then().catch()` — fire-and-forget, never blocks the bot response. ✓
- WS scoping:
  * emitToTherapist(therapistId, ...) is used for every event, never a
    broadcast. ✓ No cross-therapist leak.

**T-05 (final report accept / return)**
- Idempotency:
  * acceptReport already idempotent when status === 'accepted' (early
    return, no duplicate Telegram push). ✓
  * returnReport on an accepted report returns { conflict } → 409. ✓
  * returnReport on an already-returned report with the SAME comment
    used to re-encrypt + re-update returned_at + re-audit + RE-NOTIFY,
    which means a double-click on the modal's Submit button would send
    TWO Telegram pushes to the client. **BUG FIX #1 below.**
- Ownership:
  * Standalone /api/assignments/:id/reports/:rid/... router checks
    Number(base.therapist_id) === Number(req.user.id) before any service
    call. Attempt by therapist A to accept therapist B's client report
    returns 403 (not 500, not data leak). ✓

**T-21 (photo attachments)**
- Limits enforced (5/report, 10MB, image mime allowlist) at both layers:
  * routes/bot.js validates BEFORE service call but used to do the disk
    write before checking mime. **BUG FIX #2 below.**
  * services/assignmentReports.insertAttachment re-validates as last line
    of defense, throws { code: 'invalid_input' } on violation.
- Delete-on-disk:
  * routes/clients.js DELETE handler explicitly fs.unlinkSync(.enc) BEFORE
    calling deleteAttachment(). On-disk file removed even when service
    delete fails. ✓
- Signed access / opaque ID:
  * file_ref is crypto.randomUUID() + ext + '.enc' → unguessable. Never
    exposed to the wire; therapist streams via the authenticated route.
    Response carries 'X-Content-Type-Options: nosniff' + 'Cache-Control:
    no-store'. Bytes are not stored as-is on disk (encrypted with key
    rotation tracked via encryption_key_id + payload_version). ✓
- Frontend lightbox lifecycle:
  * Previous design: thumbnail's useEffect cleanup revoked the blob URL on
    unmount; the parent passed that same URL to the lightbox. A WS-driven
    refetch (assignment_report_accepted / _returned / attachment_added)
    could remount thumbnails and revoke the URL while the lightbox was
    still showing the full-size image — broken image until close. **BUG
    FIX #3 below.**

**T-25 (client engagement analytics)**
- Division-by-zero / single-report safety:
  * stdev() returns 0 for `< 2` values. ✓
  * meanGap / medianGap / max / minGap all guarded with
    `gapsDays.length > 0` check. ✓
  * consistencyScore returns null when `< 1` gaps (i.e. fewer than 2
    reports — matches the inline comment). ✓
- Window-aware aggregation:
  * Window capped at 365 days at the route layer (Math.min(n, 365)).
  * Window passed through to listReportsForClient as `'-N days'`, applied
    inside the SQL with datetime('now', ?). ✓
- Consent + ownership:
  * /api/clients/:id/engagement uses verifyClientConsent ('engagement')
    AND additionally verifies `WHERE id = ? AND therapist_id = ? AND
    role = 'client'` before reading anything. ✓ No URL-tampering leak.
- N+1 / perf:
  * listReportsForClient does ONE SELECT for all reports, then decrypts
    each row's content in-process to compute length. For a 1000-report
    client that's 1000 decrypt calls inside one request. Audit step 13
    flagged this as "use ciphertext_length?" — confirmed it would be a
    valid micro-optimization but is NOT a correctness bug. Not fixed in
    this audit (out of scope for a bug sweep; would be a separate
    perf-tuning feature).
- decryptRow → listAttachmentsForReport for EVERY row in
  listReportsForAssignment is an N+1 in the dashboard feed too; same
  perf-only call-out, not fixed here.

**T-26 (AI source disclaimers)**
- Migration idempotency:
  * Each `ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN` is wrapped in its own try/catch — repeat
    boots are no-ops. ✓
  * Backfill `UPDATE users SET show_ai_sources = 1 WHERE show_ai_sources
    IS NULL` is idempotent (becomes a no-op once all rows have a value).
    ✓ Verified by booting the app twice; no migration errors.
- Cross-therapist sources leak:
  * vectorStore.searchKb(query, therapistId, ...) scopes the vector
    search to the requesting therapist.
  * buildKbContext does the followup chunk lookup with
    `WHERE c.id = ? AND c.therapist_id = ?` — explicit therapist scope.
    ✓ Therapist A's hits NEVER show up in therapist B's session
    summary or exercise sources_json.
- show_ai_sources is UI-only:
  * Settings PUT only flips the column; the source data is persisted
    unconditionally by summarization/exercise-authoring. Toggling on
    after the fact brings the disclaimer back without re-running
    generation. ✓ Audit-compliant: data always stored.

**Cross-file regression**
- 3 of the 5 commits (T-04, T-05, T-21) edit
  services/assignmentReports.js. The final-state file is well-organized:
  T-04 helpers at top, T-05 accept/return in the middle, T-21
  attachment block at the bottom, T-25 analytics last. Single module
  exports object with no duplicates or shadowing.
- routes/clients.js similarly stacks T-04 → T-21 → T-25 sections cleanly.
- AssignmentsPanel.jsx has separate sub-components (ReportPhotoThumbnail,
  ReportPhotoLightbox, AssignmentReportsFeed) with no naming collisions.
- bot/index.js photo handler vs voice/text handlers all interact through
  the same activeReports[telegramId] map without stomping each other.

**i18n coverage**
- assignment.report.*           — 42 keys × 4 locales (en/ru/es/uk).
- analytics.engagement.*        — 40 keys × 4 locales (ru/uk have
                                   _few/_many plural forms in addition
                                   to _one/_other; en/es only need
                                   _one/_other per CLDR plural rules).
- clientDetail.engagementTab    —  1 key × 4 locales.
- ai.disclaimer.*               — 17 keys × 4 locales.
  Validated with a programmatic key-set diff against en.json — no
  missing translations in ru/es/uk. The only diff is the Slavic-only
  `_few` / `_many` plural forms which are correctly NOT present in
  en/es per CLDR plural rules for those locales.

### Bug fixes applied

**Fix #1 — T-05 returnReport idempotency on double-click.**
File: src/backend/src/services/assignmentReports.js (+8 lines).
Before: A second call to returnReport with the SAME comment re-encrypted,
re-stamped returned_at, re-audited, and re-sent the Telegram push to the
client. UX impact: rapid Submit-button clicks (or a slow network retry)
caused the client to receive 2+ identical "your report was returned"
pushes.
After: When `acceptance_status === 'returned'` AND
`report.therapist_comment === trimmed` (the new comment matches the
already-stored one), return early with the current state — no DB write,
no audit log, no notification. Therapists editing their feedback with a
DIFFERENT comment still get the update + re-notify (legitimate use case
preserved).
Regression test (`_t385_return_idempotent.js`): 6/6 assertions pass —
  - 1st return → 1 push
  - 2nd return (same comment) → 0 pushes
  - 3rd return (different comment) → 1 push

**Fix #2 — T-21 mime validation BEFORE disk write.**
File: src/backend/src/routes/bot.js (+12 lines).
Before: The bot upload route did the base64 decode + buffer cap check
correctly, but then proceeded to encrypt + write the file to disk before
the service-layer mime check ran inside insertAttachment(). On rejection
the orphan cleanup ran, but disk I/O + an AES-GCM encrypt had already
been spent. Could be abused by a noisy client to do many wasted writes.
After: After determining `inferredMime`, validate against
`assignmentReports.ALLOWED_ATTACHMENT_MIMES` immediately and return
400 if unsupported. Disk write only happens once the mime is on the
allowlist. Service-layer check stays as defense-in-depth.

**Fix #3 — T-21 photo lightbox owns its own blob URL fetch.**
File: src/frontend/src/components/AssignmentsPanel.jsx (~50 lines).
Before: ReportPhotoThumbnail created an `URL.createObjectURL` blob URL
on mount, passed it through `onOpen(blobUrl)` → parent's setLightboxUrl
→ lightbox `<img src={blobUrl}>`. The thumbnail's useEffect cleanup
revoked the URL on unmount. If the AssignmentReportsFeed refetched
(WS tick from assignment_report_accepted / _returned / attachment_added)
while the lightbox was open, the thumbnail could remount and revoke the
URL, breaking the open lightbox image.
After: Lightbox accepts a `streamUrl` (the authenticated stream-route
URL) instead of a blob URL, runs its own fetch + createObjectURL +
revoke cleanup. Thumbnail's lifecycle is now fully independent of the
lightbox's. The parent passes the streamUrl string when opening; the
lightbox owns the blob from fetch to unmount.

### Verification (YOLO mode)

1. `node --check` on every backend file touched by the audit:
     - src/backend/src/services/assignmentReports.js   OK
     - src/backend/src/routes/bot.js                   OK
     - src/backend/src/routes/clients.js               OK
     - src/backend/src/routes/assignments.js           OK
     - src/backend/src/db/connection.js                OK
     - src/backend/src/utils/telegramNotify.js         OK
     - src/bot/src/index.js                            OK
   All seven files parse clean.

2. Frontend production build:
   `npm --prefix src/frontend run build` succeeded in 2.28s — 1086
   modules, 1.36 MB main bundle gzipped to 380 KB. Zero build errors
   after the lightbox refactor.

3. End-to-end smoke (`_t385_smoke.js`):
   Seeds therapist + client + assignment, drives:
     - T-04 text report create/round-trip
     - T-21 attach photo + per-report cap (5) + mime rejection
     - T-05 final report → return (without/short/valid comment) →
            re-create final → accept → completed → conflict on re-return
     - T-25 engagement aggregator on multi-report + 0-report clients
     - T-26 buildKbContext envelope shape
   41/41 assertions pass. Telegram-notify lines render in dev-mode logs
   exactly as expected.

4. Idempotent return regression test (`_t385_return_idempotent.js`):
   6/6 assertions pass. Spied Telegram send counter goes 1 → 0 → 1
   across the three return calls.

5. i18n key coverage script (custom): all four locales have full
   coverage of the T-04/T-05/T-21/T-25/T-26 prefixes after accounting
   for CLDR plural form differences (en/es have _one/_other; ru/uk
   additionally have _few/_many).

### What was NOT fixed (deliberately scoped out)

- N+1 attachments listing inside decryptRow (perf only; not a
  correctness bug).
- N+1 plaintext-length decryption in T-25 listReportsForClient
  (perf only; using ciphertext_length would be a separate optimization).

## Session 2026-05-18 — Feature #386: Regression sweep: auth and session flows

### Scope
Regression audit of all authentication and session flows: registration,
login, logout, JWT/CSRF handling, password reset, invite code, rate
limiting, log sanitization. 70-assertion API audit script + browser
automation end-to-end.

### API audit results (70/70 pass)

Step 2 Registration:
  - No CSRF token on POST -> 403 (enforcement working)
  - Invalid email -> 400; weak password (no uppercase) -> 400
  - Valid registration -> 201; cookie: HttpOnly, SameSite=Strict, no
    Secure in dev (correct); JWT in response body
  - Duplicate email -> 409; client role -> 400 (blocked)

Step 3 Login:
  - No CSRF -> 403; wrong password -> 401 "Invalid credentials"
  - Non-existent email -> same 401 (no user enumeration)
  - Valid login -> 200 + JWT + HttpOnly SameSite=Strict cookie

Step 4 /api/auth/me:
  - No token -> 401; valid token -> 200; invalid JWT -> 401

Step 5 CSRF behavior:
  - Each GET /api/csrf-token returns a unique 64-hex token
  - Invalid token on POST -> 403
  - Requests with Authorization: Bearer bypass CSRF (design intent)

Step 6 Logout:
  - POST /api/auth/logout -> 200, clears session_token cookie

Step 7 Password reset:
  - Non-existent email -> generic 200 (no enumeration)
  - Invalid token -> 400; weak new password -> 400
  - Valid reset -> 200; token one-time-use (reuse -> 400)
  - Login with new password -> 200; old password -> 401

Step 8 Invite code:
  - GET /api/invite-code without auth -> 401
  - GET /api/invite-code -> 200, 8-char code
  - GET /api/invite-code/link -> 200, Telegram deep-link
  - POST /api/invite-code/regenerate -> 200, new distinct code

Step 9 Rate limiting:
  - Rate-limit headers present on auth responses (limit: 1000 in dev)

Step 10 Log sanitization:
  - No plaintext passwords in logs
  - No raw JWT cookie values in logs
  - Password reset link logged in dev mode (auth.js:738, intentional)

Step 11 Protected routes:
  - /api/clients, /api/sessions/list -> 401 without auth

### Real bug found and fixed: useCsrfToken destructuring error (4 files)

Root cause: useCsrfToken() returns { csrfToken, isLoading }. Four files
called `const csrfToken = useCsrfToken()` without destructuring, assigning
the whole object. Then `headers['X-CSRF-Token'] = csrfToken` set the
header to "[object Object]" -> backend returned 403.

Impact:
  - ForgotPassword.jsx: forgot-password form always got 403 in the browser
  - ResetPassword.jsx: same 403 on password reset
  - ExerciseLibrary.jsx: broken CSRF on library form submissions
  - AssistantChatPanel.jsx: object passed to callbacks

Fix applied to 4 files:
  - const csrfToken = useCsrfToken()
  + const { csrfToken, isLoading: csrfLoading } = useCsrfToken()
  Also: disabled={loading || csrfLoading} on submit buttons in
  ForgotPassword and ResetPassword (matching Login/Register pattern).

Verification:
  - grep for bad pattern in src/frontend/src/ -> 0 results
  - npm --prefix src/frontend run build -> success (1086 modules, 0 errors)
  - Browser automation:
      Register -> Dashboard
      Logout -> landing page
      Forgot password form -> success banner (was 403, now fixed)
      Reset password with valid token -> success
      Login with new post-reset password -> Dashboard

### Files changed
  src/frontend/src/pages/ForgotPassword.jsx    (+3/-3)
  src/frontend/src/pages/ResetPassword.jsx     (+3/-3)
  src/frontend/src/pages/ExerciseLibrary.jsx   (+1/-1)
  src/frontend/src/components/AssistantChatPanel.jsx (+1/-1)

### Current status
- Feature #386: PASSING (auth regression sweep — 70/70 API checks pass;
  real CSRF-destructuring bug found in 4 frontend files and fixed; browser
  UI tested end-to-end across registration, login, logout, forgot-password,
  reset-password; invite code deep-link verified; rate-limit headers confirmed).
- Stats: 386/397 features passing (97.2%).
- Stats: 385/385 features passing (100%).

## Session 2026-05-18 — Feature #387: Regression sweep: consent enforcement on client data routes

### Scope
Regression audit confirming consent gating still blocks unauthorized access to client diary,
notes, transcripts, and summaries after recent code changes.

### What was verified (42/42 assertions)

**Step 1 — REST reads WITHOUT consent → 403:**
  GET /diary, /context, /sessions, /exercises, POST /notes, PUT /context,
  POST /exercises (send) — all return 403 when consent_therapist_access=0

**Step 4 — Signed-file stream without consent → 403:**
  - Bot creates diary text entry (client write, no consent needed)
  - GET /diary/:id/stream with linked-but-no-consent therapist → 403
  - POST /assignments/.../attachments/.../stream → 403 before 404

**Grant → revoke mid-session (Step 2):**
  - bot/consent grant → 200, all routes now return 200
  - bot/revoke-consent → 200, all routes immediately return 403 again
  - Notes list: 200 after revoke (design-intent: therapist retains read of own notes)

**Step 5 — WebSocket:**
  - Valid therapist JWT → 'connected' message (no consent gate needed, push-only)
  - Invalid JWT → close code 4001

**Step 8 — Cross-therapist isolation:**
  - Therapist B cannot read therapist A's client data (diary, context, notes, stream) → 403

**Step 3 — Export consent gate:**
  - GET /export/client/:id?format=json → 403 when consent=0

**Step 9 — SOS bypass (design intent):**
  - GET /clients/:id/sos with consent=0 but linked → 200 (emergency access by design)

**Steps 6 & 7 — Audit log verification:**
  - 15 access_denied entries for therapist A, all with reason=consent_not_granted

## Session 2026-05-18 — Feature #393: Regression sweep: search (vector + NL query expansion)

### Scope
End-to-end regression audit of semantic vector search and Pro/Premium NL query expansion.
All 4 feature verification steps covered via a 56-assertion audit script
(_t393_search_audit.js) plus browser UI verification.

### Real bug found and fixed: revoked-consent data leaked in global search

**Root cause:** semanticSearch() in vectorStore.js filtered by therapist_id but NOT by
consent_therapist_access. When a client revoked consent, the bot set therapist_id=NULL
and consent_therapist_access=0 on the user row, but the embedding in vector_embeddings
still had the old therapist_id. A global search (no client_id filter) would return
these stale embeddings — exposing data from clients who explicitly revoked consent.

**Fix applied:** src/backend/src/routes/search.js — post-search consent filter added.
After semanticSearch() returns results, collect unique client_ids, query which ones still
have therapist_id = currentTherapist AND consent_therapist_access = 1, and filter out
any results from clients not in that consented set. KB chunks (client_id=NULL) always kept.

### Audit results (56/56 assertions)

**Step 1 — Re-index test corpus and run baseline vector queries:**
  - 6 diary entries + 1 therapist note created and auto-indexed
  - GET /api/search/stats -> 200, total > 0, diary_entry type present
  - POST /api/search with compound-key query -> results with similarity score, source_type
  - POST /api/search with client_id filter -> narrows to that client's data
  - POST /api/search with source_type=diary_entry -> all results are diary_entry
  - Invalid source_type -> 400; empty query -> 400; >1000 char query -> 400
  - No auth -> 403 (CSRF check before auth for POST); GET stats without auth -> 401
  - Therapist A does NOT see Therapist B's data (therapist_id isolation confirmed)
  - Vector search latency < 500ms (got 88ms)

**Step 2 — NL query tier gating:**
  - Basic plan -> 403 with current_plan='basic', required_plans=['pro','premium']
  - Trial plan -> 403 (default post-registration)
  - Pro plan -> passes tier gate; 404 for nonexistent client (not 403)
  - Premium plan -> passes tier gate
  - Real NL query "anxiety depression sleep": total_matches > 0
  - expanded_terms includes synonyms for 'anxiety' (anxious, worry, panic, fear...)
  - expanded_terms includes synonyms for 'sleep' (insomnia, nightmare, tired, fatigue...)
  - Results include diary and/or note entries; similarity_score in [0,1]
  - query_tokens returned; includes 'anxiety'; search_time_ms present
  - NL query latency < 500ms (got 156ms)

**Step 3 — Consent filtering (includes bug fix verification):**
  - Consented client_id search -> 200
  - Other therapist's client by client_id -> 403
  - Data IS found BEFORE consent revocation
  - After revocation: global search -> 0 results (consent filter bug FIXED)
  - After revocation: explicit client_id -> 403
  - NL query for revoked client -> 403 or 404 (unlinked)
  - Cross-therapist NL isolation -> 404
  - Audit log: semantic_search and nl_query events recorded

**Step 4 — Latency baseline:**
  - Vector search: 88ms < 500ms
  - NL query: 156ms < 500ms
  - Stats endpoint: 44ms < 200ms

**Mock data grep:** Zero hits across search.js, query.js, vectorStore.js, nlQuery.js.

### Browser UI verification
  - Logged into dashboard: Pro Plan badge shown, zero JS console errors
  - Clients page: real data (0 clients for fresh account), Pro limit=30 shown

### Files changed
  src/backend/src/routes/search.js   — post-search consent filter added (+28 lines)
  _t393_search_audit.js              — 56-assertion regression audit
  _t393_debug.js                     — consent filter debug helper
  _t393_browser_login.js             — browser test account helper

## Session 2026-05-19 — Feature #395: Regression sweep: admin panel and audit logs

## Session 2026-05-19 — Feature #4: No mock data patterns in codebase

### Scope
Static analysis scan of the entire codebase for prohibited mock/placeholder data
patterns. All 7 grep checks from the feature spec run via ripgrep (which respects
.gitignore and excludes node_modules).

### Grep results

**CHECK 1 — globalThis.:** No matches ✅
**CHECK 2 — devStore|DevStore|dev-store|mockDb|mock-db:** No matches ✅
**CHECK 3 — mockData|testData|fakeData|sampleData|dummyData:** No matches ✅
**CHECK 4 — TODO.*real|TODO.*database|TODO.*API|STUB|MOCK:** No matches ✅
**CHECK 5 — isDevelopment|isDev|process.env.NODE_ENV.*development:** No matches ✅
**CHECK 6 — new Map()|new Set():** 22 matches — investigated, ALL LEGITIMATE (see below)
**CHECK 7 — json-server|miragejs|msw in package.json:** No matches ✅

### Check 6 investigation (new Map / new Set)

All 22 hits investigated and confirmed as legitimate JavaScript patterns:

**Rate limiters (5 instances) — correctly ephemeral:**
  - assistant.js: rateLimitMap (max 30 msg/min per therapist)
  - auth.js: forgotPasswordRates (forgot-password rate window)
  - publicAssistant.js: publicRateLimitMap
  - emailService.js: rateLimitMap (email send rate limiting)
  - bot/index.js: voiceForwardRateLimit (max 10 voice/min per therapist)

**Runtime connection/state tracking — must be in-memory:**
  - websocketService.js: therapistConnections (active WS sessions, ephemeral by nature)
  - bot.js: recentSosClients (5-min SOS dedup window)

**CSRF token store — correctly ephemeral with 2hr TTL + cleanup:**
  - csrf.js: csrfTokens (synchronizer token pattern, cleaned up every 30min)

**Frontend event management — must be in-memory (browser runtime state):**
  - useWebSocket.js: globalListeners, connectSubscribers (React event subscriptions)

**Local function/request variables — per-request computation only:**
  - sessions.js: clientsById, sessionsByDate, seenClient
  - assignmentReports.js: dayBuckets
  - assistantKnowledge.js: processedFiles
  - clients.js: existingEmails, seenEmails
  - vectorStore.js: tokenBuckets, privateDiaryIds

**Conclusion:** Zero instances of in-memory data stores used as database
replacements. All persistent application data (users, sessions, diary entries,
exercises, subscriptions, audit logs, etc.) is stored in SQLite via better-sqlite3.
The Map/Set uses are all for ephemeral runtime state (rate limiting, active
connections, per-request aggregation, frontend events) where in-memory is the
correct and only viable approach.

### Additional finding: null byte in kbIngest.js
Binary grep detected a null byte at byte ~6809 in kbIngest.js. The file parses
correctly (Node.js can load it; 495 lines, 18275 bytes). The `new Map()` use
in kbIngest.js (line 430, `bestPerKb`) is a local KB source deduplication
variable — confirmed legitimate.

### Feature status
Feature #4 was already marked passing (confirmed by feature_mark_passing error).
Investigation confirms the passing status is correct.

### Current status
- Feature #4: PASSING — all 7 grep checks pass, 22 Map/Set hits investigated and confirmed legitimate

## Session 2026-05-19 — Feature #396: Pre-release smoke test Docker Compose stack on staging

### Scope
Pre-release smoke test verifying the full 6-service Docker Compose stack configuration
and a complete happy-path scenario end-to-end. Audit script: _t396_docker_smoke_test.js
(98 assertions).

### Bugs found and fixed

**Bug 1: nginx service MISSING from docker-compose.yml**
  The docker-compose.yml defined only 5 services (backend, frontend, bot, umami, umami-db).
  The nginx reverse proxy (6th service per PRD) was completely absent. Added it with:
  ports 80:80 and 443:443; config files mounted; nginx-certs volume; depends_on chain.

**Bug 2: Wrong analytics path in nginx/locations.conf**
  locations.conf had `location /umami/` instead of `/analytics/` per PRD spec.
  Fixed: renamed to `location /analytics/` and updated APP_BASE_PATH comment.

**Bug 3: Umami missing APP_BASE_PATH env var**
  Umami container had no APP_BASE_PATH so it served at / instead of /analytics/.
  Fixed: added APP_BASE_PATH=/analytics to Umami environment in docker-compose.
  Also updated Umami healthcheck path to /analytics/api/heartbeat.

**Bug 4: Umami tracking script using hardcoded production URL**
  src/frontend/index.html loaded Umami from https://app.pr-top.com/script.js (hardcoded).
  This bypassed the nginx reverse proxy, defeating AdBlock avoidance per PRD.
  Fixed: changed to /analytics/script.js (relative URL through nginx proxy).

**Bug 5: Missing nginx-certs volume declaration**
  nginx service mounted nginx-certs volume but it was not declared in volumes block.
  Fixed: added nginx-certs: to the volumes section.

### Audit results (98/98 pass)

**Step 1 - Docker Compose configuration:**
  All 6 services present (nginx+backend+frontend+bot+umami+umami-db)
  nginx exposes ports 80 and 443; config files correctly mounted
  SSL certs volume defined; APP_BASE_PATH=/analytics; healthchecks configured

**Step 2 - GET /api/health returns 200:**
  status ok, database connected, version present, websocket and stripe info present

**Step 3 - Nginx routing configuration:**
  Upstreams: frontend:80, backend:3001, umami:3000 all defined
  /api/ to backend (WebSocket upgrade headers + 120s timeouts)
  /analytics/ to umami (rate limited 10 req/s)
  / to frontend (catch-all SPA fallback)
  Security headers and rate limiting configured; old /umami/ path removed

**Step 4 - SSL/TLS configuration:**
  HTTPS server block (port 443) present in nginx.conf (commented pending cert)
  ssl_certificate, ssl_certificate_key, TLS 1.2/1.3, SSL session cache, OCSP stapling
  HSTS header configured; Let's Encrypt paths configured

**Step 5 - Happy-path scenario (fully verified end-to-end):**
  GET /api/csrf-token -> 200; POST /api/auth/register -> 201; GET /api/invite-code -> 200
  POST /api/bot/register -> 201; POST /api/bot/connect -> 200; POST /api/bot/consent -> 200
  GET /api/clients -> 200 (connected client visible)
  POST /api/bot/diary -> 201; GET /api/clients/:id/diary -> 200 (content decrypted)
  POST /api/bot/sos -> 201; GET /api/clients/:id/sos -> 200 (SOS list non-empty)
  POST /api/sessions/ (multipart audio) -> 201
  POST /api/sessions/:id/transcribe -> 200
  POST /api/sessions/:id/summarize -> 200
  GET /api/sessions/:id/summary -> 200 (summary text non-empty)
  GET /api/sessions/:id/stream (Range) -> 206 (Accept-Ranges: bytes)
  DELETE /api/sessions/:id -> 200

**Step 6 - Umami analytics configuration:**
  APP_BASE_PATH=/analytics confirmed; index.html uses /analytics/script.js
  /analytics/ routing confirmed in locations.conf; old /umami/ path removed

### Browser UI verification
  - Landing page: "Keep Your Practice on Top" renders correctly, zero real JS errors
  - Expected dev-mode: /analytics/script.js returns 404 (correct - Umami not running
    in dev, resolves in Docker production with nginx active)

### Note on Docker daemon
  Docker Desktop was not running during this session, so actual `docker compose up -d`
  could not be executed. All configuration and API behavior was verified through the
  running dev server. Full Docker brings-up test requires Docker Desktop running.

### Files changed
  docker-compose.yml          added nginx service, Umami APP_BASE_PATH, nginx-certs volume
  nginx/locations.conf        /umami/ to /analytics/ path fix
  src/frontend/index.html     Umami script changed from hardcoded URL to /analytics/script.js
  _t396_docker_smoke_test.js  98-assertion smoke test script

### Current status

  idx_srd_session (session_id)
  uq_srd_session_offset_channel UNIQUE (session_id, offset_minutes, channel)
                                  -- structural dedup against cron overlap

All ALTER TABLE statements wrapped in try/catch (idempotent re-run safe).

### #400 — reminderService: planner + dispatchers + cancel-pending
Created src/backend/src/services/reminderService.js (~590 LOC) with:

  computeWallClockTargets(scheduledAtIso, tz)   -- pure, DST-safe target math
  planForSession(sessionId)                     -- INSERT OR IGNORE dispatches
  dispatchOptInNotices()                        -- 3C-strict opt-in (Telegram bot button)
  dispatchDue()                                 -- process pending with re-read +
                                                   quiet-hours skip + audit
  cancelPendingForSession(sessionId, reason)    -- supersede on reschedule/cancel
  markNoShows()                                 -- soft-default after grace window

Key behaviour:
  - DST-safe: uses Intl.DateTimeFormat with timeZone for IANA-aware conversion
    (matches the helper in routes/clients.js:29-81).
  - Idempotent re-plan: unique index uq_srd_session_offset_channel + pre-check.
  - Race-safe dispatch: re-reads session.attendance_status immediately before
    send so a client confirmation mid-flight produces 'superseded' not a wasted send.
  - Quiet-hours respected: reads escalation_preferences.quiet_hours_* of the CLIENT
    (not therapist) -- cross-midnight windows handled correctly.
  - Channel resolution: telegram if telegram_id set, email if email set; both if both.
  - Dev mode safe: when TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN unset, telegramNotify logs instead of
    sending, and dispatcher counts as 'sent' (so we don't retry forever locally).
  - Audit log every state change ('session_reminder_sent' / '_failed' / '_superseded' /
    'session_reminder_optin_asked' / 'session_marked_no_show').

Wall-clock target rules (architecture section 4.1 #2):
  Target A: day-before @ 09:00 client local.
  Target B: prefer day-of @ 09:00 client local; fall back to scheduled-2h
            if 09:00 is inside the 2h pre-window OR already passed (provided
            scheduled-2h is itself still in the future).
  Skip any target whose UTC instant is already past or after the session.

Verification (_t400_reminder_service.js + _t400_reminder_dispatch.js):
  Unit (pure fn):   17/17 incl. normal case, sub-24h skip, early-morning
                            fallback, in-past skip, sub-2h skip, DST spring-forward
                            (America/New_York 2026-03-08), label stability.
  Integration:      11/11 incl. 25h-future fixture, idempotent re-plan,
                            opt-out skip, cancelPendingForSession 4-to-0 pending,
                            markNoShows + idempotent re-run.
  Helpers:           6/6 incl. cross-midnight quiet hours, SQLite-format parseIso.
  Dispatch e2e:      8/8 incl. pending-to-sent transition, audit row created,
                            confirmed-to-superseded, not-opted-in-to-skipped.
  TOTAL: 45/45 assertions across the two scripts.
